There is a great deal of academic literature on the European Union, but not so many reliable books for the general reader or for 
those who are just setting out to acquire academic knowledge. 

Of the many texts that provide [1mgeneral introductions [0m, two good options are Desmond Dinanโs [3mEver Closer Union [0m(Basingstoke, 4th 
edn, 2010, 640 pp.) and John McCormickโs [3mUnderstanding the EU [0m(Basingstoke, 5th edn, 2011, 264 pp.). A federalist view of the way 
in which the EU has developed is to be found in Michael Burgess, [3mFederalism and European Union: The Building of Europe, 1950โ2000 [0m
(London, 2000, 290 pp.). Chapters on all the main policies are to be found in Helen Wallace, Mark Pollack, and Alisdair Young 
(eds), [3mPolicy-Making in the European Union [0m(Oxford, 6th edn, 2010, 640 pp.). A wide range of subjects is also covered in the [3m
Annual Review of the Journal of Common Market Studies [0m(Oxford). 

Timothy Bainbridge and Anthony Teasdale, [3mThe Penguin Companion to the European Union [0m(Harmondsworth, 3rd edn, 2012, 880 pp.) is an 
accurate and convenient [1mwork of reference [0m. For those who appreciate a [1mbiographical [0mapproach to the subject, the history of the EC 
up to the 1970s is seen through the eyes of its principal founding father in Jean Monnetโs [3mMemoirs [0m(London, 1978, 544 pp.). 
Flavour and substance of the Delors period, from 1985 to 1994, are to be found in Charles Grant, [3mInside the House that Jacques 
Built [0m(London, 1994, 305 pp.). A range of leading actors in the uniting of Europe are given lively treatment in Martyn Bond, Julie 
Smith, and William Wallace (eds), [3mEminent Europeans [0m(London, 1996, 321 pp.). Hugo Young provides unsurpassed insights into the 
development of British relations with the EU, through chapters on a dozen British protagonists and antagonists from Churchill to 
Blair, in [3mThis Blessed Plot [0m(Basingstoke, 1998, 558 pp.). 

There is not much that is easy to read and gives a true and fair view of how the [1minstitutions [0mwork. Neil Nugentโs [3mThe Government 
and Politics of the European Union [0m(Basingstoke, 7th edn, 2010, 512 pp.) is reliable and comprehensive, but not light reading. 
Michelle Cini and Nieves Perez-Solorzano Borraganโs [3mEuropean Union Politics [0m(Oxford, 3rd edn, 2010, 520 pp.) opens up a wide range 
of subjects to the reader. John Peterson and Michael Shackletonโs [3mThe Institutions of the European Union [0m(Oxford, 3rd edn, 2012, 
472 pp.) is a very good overview. Shorter explanations of the institutions can be found in the chapter on โInstitutions or 
Constitutionโ in [3mThe Building of the European Union [0mand in Helen Wallaceโs chapter on โAn Institutional Anatomy and Five Policy 
Modesโ in Wallace, Pollack, and Young (eds), [3mPolicy-Making in the European Union [0m(both books cited above). Chapters 7โ10 of 
Dinanโs [3mEver Closer Union [0m(also cited above) deal with main institutions. 

Ali El-Agraaโs [3mThe European Union: Economics and Policies [0m(Cambridge, 9th edn, 2011, 518 pp.) has the most current overview of [1m
economics and economic policies [0m. Lord Cockfieldโs [3mThe European Union: Creating the Single Market [0m(Chichester, 1994, 185 pp.) is a 
lucid and entertaining account by the man who did most to create it, while Alasdair Young, in โThe Single Marketโ (chapter in 
Wallace, Pollack, and Young (eds), [3mPolicy-Making in the European Union [0m), brings you up to date. The budget is well explained by 
Brigid Laffan and Johannes Lindner (chapter in Wallace, Pollack, and Young (eds), [3mPolicy-Making in the European Union [0m). A useful 
summary of the EUโs environmental policies is given in Andrew Jordan and Camilla Adelle (eds), [3mEnvironmental Policy in the EU: 
Actors, Institutions and Processes [0m(Abingdon, 2012, 424 pp.). 

Most of the literature on the EUโs [1mexternal relations [0mis about the Common Foreign and Security Policy, though the external 
economic policies remain more effective and important. Fraser Cameron gives a wide-ranging overview in An [3mIntroduction to European 
Foreign Policy [0m(Abingdon, 2012, 320 pp.), with Stephan Keukeleire and Jennifer MacNaughtanโs more detailed [3mThe Foreign Policy of 
the European Union [0m(Basingstoke, 2008, 392 pp.) working as a companion. 

The [1mArea of Freedom, Security, and Justice [0mis also a fast-moving subject: Sandra Lavenexโs chapter on โJustice and Home Affairsโ 
in Wallace, Pollack, and Young (eds), [3mPolicy-Making in [0mgives a good overview. 

[1mAcross the board, [0mthe EUโs websiteโhttp://europa.euโis a vast quarry of information, from the very basic through to the highly 
technical.
